# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Firefox DOM Event Dispatch Chain

## Your Task

Trace how a DOM event (e.g., click) is dispatched through the Firefox event system in mozilla/gecko-dev. Find C++ source files implementing: the event creation, the event target identification, the capture/bubble phase traversal, the event listener invocation, and the default action execution.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossrepo domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/firefox--871325b8.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/firefox--871325b8` (mozilla-firefox/firefox)

```json
}
```

Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

Excellent! I've successfully traced the complete Firefox DOM event dispatch system and created a comprehensive analysis file at `/workspace/answer.json`.

## Summary of Findings

I've documented the complete event dispatch flow in Firefox, identifying **15 core implementation files** and **20 key symbols** that implement the event system:

### Key Components:

**1. Event Creation** (`dom/events/EventDispatcher.cpp`)
- `EventDispatcher::Dispatch()` and `DispatchDOMEvent()` - Main entry points
- Creates or accepts DOM Event objects that wrap low-level `WidgetEvent` structures

**2. Event Target Chain Building** 
- Recursively calls `GetEventTargetParent()` on each target starting from the original target up through parents
- Implementations in `dom/base/FragmentOrElement.cpp`, `Document.cpp`, and element-specific files
- Handles event retargeting (crucial for Shadow DOM)

**3. Capture Phase** (`EventTargetChainItem::HandleEventTargetChain()`)
- Iterates **backwards** through the event target chain
- Sets `mInCapturePhase = true`
- Invokes listeners registered in capture mode

**4. Event Listener Invocation** (`EventListenerManager.cpp`)
- `HandleEventInternal()` - Retrieves listeners and dispatches them
- `HandleEventSingleListener()` - Invokes individual listeners (WebIDL or XPCOM)
- Manages listener compilation, error handling, and passive listener tracking

**5. Bubble Phase** 
- After target phase, iterates **forwards** through the chain
- Sets `mInBubblingPhase = true`
- Only fires if event has `mBubbles = true`
- Respects propagation stops and preventDefault

**6. Default Action Execution**
- `ActivationBehavior()` called after dispatch completes
- Element-specific implementations (HTMLInputElement, HTMLButtonElement, etc.)
- Performs actions like form submission, l
... (truncated)

`EventDispatcher::Dispatch()` or `EventDispatcher::DispatchDOMEvent()`. These methods accept a `WidgetEvent*` (the low-level event) and optionally a `dom::Event*` (the DOM-facing event). If a DOM Event is not provided, one is created lazily during dispatch using `EventDispatcher::CreateEvent()`.\\n\\n## Event Target Identification and Chain Building\\nThe event dispatcher constructs an event target chain by iteratively calling `GetEventTargetParent()` on each potential target, starting from the original target and moving up through parent targets. This process is implemented through:\\n\\n- **`EventTargetChainItem::GetEventTargetParent()` (dom/events/EventDispatcher.cpp:429-444)**: Calls the target's `GetEventTargetParent()` method and caches properties like whether the target wants pre/post-handle events.\\n- **Target-specific implementations** in `dom/base/FragmentOrElement.cpp`, `dom/base/Document.cpp`, `dom/base/nsWindowRoot.cpp`, and element-specific files like `dom/html/HTMLInputElement.cpp` that override `GetEventTargetParent()` to set the parent target and handle retargeting (especially important for shadow DOM and anonymous content).\\n\\nThe chain building continues through a while loop in `Dispatch()` (lines 1113-1178) that calls `GetEventTargetParent()` on successive parent targets until no more parents are available or a target indicates it cannot handle the event.\\n\\n## Capture Phase Dispatch\\nOnce the event target chain is built, event dispatch occurs in `EventTargetChainItem::HandleEventTargetChain()` (dom/events/EventDispatcher.cpp:491-694). Calls the target's `WillHandleEvent()` if registered\\n2. Retrieves the target's `EventListenerManager` via `mTarget->GetExistingListenerManager()`\\n3. Calls `EventListenerManager::HandleEvent()` which delegates to `HandleEventInternal()` (dom/events/EventListenerManager.cpp:1439-1534)\\n\\n`HandleEventInternal()` performs the actual listener lookup and invocation:\\n- Retrieves listeners for the event type from the listener map\\n- Calls `HandleEventWithListenerArray()` for each listener array\\n- For each listener, invokes `HandleEventSingleListener()` (lines 1233-1295) which:\\n  - Compiles any string-based event handlers\\n  - Calls the listener's `HandleEvent()` method (either WebIDL callback or XPCOM interface)\\n  - Checks for propagation stops and exceptions\\n\\n## Target Phase Dispatch\\nAfter the capture phase completes, the event reaches the target itself (lines 587-611):\\n\\n```cpp\\n// Lines 587-611: Target phase\\naVisitor.mEvent->mFlags.mInTargetPhase = true;\\nEventTargetChainItem& targetItem = chain[firstCanHandleEventTargetIdx];\\nif (!aVisitor.mEvent->PropagationStopped() && ...) {\\n  targetItem.HandleEvent(aVisitor, aCd); It occurs in two places:\\n\\n1. **After bubble phase in default event group** (lines 1334-1347): If the event has an activation target (determined during chain building via `mWantsActivationBehavior` in `GetEventTargetParent()`), the dispatcher calls:\\n   - `LegacyCanceledActivationBehavior()` if the event was canceled\\n   - `ActivationBehavior()` if the event was not canceled\\n\\n   These methods delegate to target-specific implementations like `HTMLInputElement::ActivationBehavior()` (dom/html/HTMLInputElement.cpp) or `HTMLButtonElement::ActivationBehavior()` (dom/html/HTMLButtonElement.cpp).\\n\\n2. **In PostHandleEvent()** (dom/events/EventDispatcher.cpp:483-489): Called during the system event group dispatch. Element implementations like `Element::PostHandleEventForLinks()` (dom/base/Element.cpp:4318+) or `HTMLInputElement::PostHandleEvent()` (dom/html/HTMLInputElement.cpp:3896+) perform default actions such as navigating links or submitting forms.\\n\\n## System Event Group Dispatch\\nAfter the default event group completes, if the event is eligible, the dispatcher repeats the entire capture/target/bubble cycle for the system event group (lines 651-693). This is used for privileged, system-level event listeners that should not be affected by content listeners stopping propagation.\\n\\n## Key Files and Roles\\n\\n- **dom/events/EventDispatcher.cpp/h**: Main dispatcher orchestrating the entire flow\\n- **dom/events/EventListenerManager.cpp**: Manages registered listeners and invokes them\\n- **dom/events/Event.cpp**: DOM Event object (wraps WidgetEvent)\\n- **dom/events/EventStateManager.cpp**: Pre/post-event state management\\n- **dom/base/Element.cpp, Document.cpp, FragmentOrElement.cpp**: Event target implementations\\n- **dom/html/HTMLInputElement.cpp, HTMLButtonElement.cpp, etc.**: Element-specific event handling and default actions\\n- **layout/base/PresShell.cpp**: Integration point for layout-triggered events\\n- **widget/nsIWidget.cpp**: Platform widget event dispatch\\n\\nThe event dispatch chain ensures proper isolation of event phases, respects propagation stops, handles event retargeting for shadow DOM, and provides clear separation between listener invocation and default action execution.\"\n}\n",

Firefox DOM Event Dispatch Chain\\n\\n## Event Creation\\nWhen a DOM event is dispatched in Firefox, the process begins in `dom/events/EventDispatcher.cpp` with the static methods `EventDispatcher::Dispatch()` or `EventDispatcher::DispatchDOMEvent()`. These methods accept a `WidgetEvent*` (the low-level event) and optionally a `dom::Event*` (the DOM-facing event). If a DOM Event is not provided, one is created lazily during dispatch using `EventDispatcher::CreateEvent()`.\\n\\n## Event Target Identification and Chain Building\\nThe event dispatcher constructs an event target chain by iteratively calling `GetEventTargetParent()` on each potential target, starting from the original target and moving up through parent targets. This process is implemented through:\\n\\n- **`EventTargetChainItem::GetEventTargetParent()` (dom/events/EventDispatcher.cpp:429-444)**: Calls the target's `GetEventTargetParent()` method and caches properties like whether the target wants pre/post-handle events.\\n- **Target-specific implementations** in `dom/base/FragmentOrElement.cpp`, `dom/base/Document.cpp`, `dom/base/nsWindowRoot.cpp`, and element-specific files like `dom/html/HTMLInputElement.cpp` that override `GetEventTargetParent()` to set the parent target and handle retargeting (especially important for shadow DOM and anonymous content).\\n\\nThe chain building continues through a while loop in `Dispatch()` (lines 1113-1178) that calls `GetEventTargetParent()` on successive parent targets until no more parents are available or a target indicates it cannot handle the event.\\n\\n## Capture Phase Dispatch\\nOnce the event target chain is built, event dispatch occurs in `EventTargetChainItem::HandleEventTargetChain()` (dom/events/EventDispatcher.cpp:491-694). The capture phase is implemented as:\\n\\n```cpp\\n// Lines 516-585: Capture phase\\naVisitor.mEvent->mFlags.mInCapturePhase = true;\\naVisitor.mEvent->mFlags.mInBubblingPhase = false;\\nfor (uint32_t i = chainLength - 1; i > firstCanHandleEventTargetIdx; --i) {\\n  EventTargetChainItem& item = chain[i];\\n  // ... event listener invocation ...\\n  item.HandleEvent(aVisitor, aCd);\\n}\\n```\\n\\nThe capture phase iterates BACKWARDS through the event target chain (from the outermost parent down to just before the target), allowing handlers registered in the capture phase to intercept the event before it reaches the target.\\n\\n## Event Listener Invocation\\nListener invocation occurs in `EventTargetChainItem::HandleEvent()` (dom/events/EventDispatcher.cpp:339-370), which:\\n\\n1. Calls the target's `WillHandleEvent()` if registered\\n2. Retrieves the target's `EventListenerManager` via `mTarget->GetExistingListenerManager()`\\n3. Calls `EventListenerManager::HandleEvent()` which delegates to `HandleEventInternal()` (dom/events/EventListenerManager.cpp:1439-1534)\\n\\n`HandleEventInternal()` performs the actual listener lookup and invocation:\\n- Retrieves listeners for the event type from the listener map\\n- Calls `HandleEventWithListenerArray()` for each listener array\\n- For each listener, invokes `HandleEventSingleListener()` (lines 1233-1295) which:\\n  - Compiles any string-based event handlers\\n  - Calls the listener's `HandleEvent()` method (either WebIDL callback or XPCOM interface)\\n  - Checks for propagation stops and exceptions\\n\\n## Target Phase Dispatch\\nAfter the capture phase completes, the event reaches the target itself (lines 587-611):\\n\\n```cpp\\n// Lines 587-611: Target phase\\naVisitor.mEvent->mFlags.mInTargetPhase = true;\\nEventTargetChainItem& targetItem = chain[firstCanHandleEventTargetIdx];\\nif (!aVisitor.mEvent->PropagationStopped() && ...) {\\n  targetItem.HandleEvent(aVisitor, aCd); It occurs in two places:\\n\\n1. **After bubble phase in default event group** (lines 1334-1347): If the event has an activation target (determined during chain building via `mWantsActivationBehavior` in `GetEventTargetParent()`), the dispatcher calls:\\n   - `LegacyCanceledActivationBehavior()` if the event was canceled\\n   - `ActivationBehavior()` if the event was not canceled\\n\\n   These methods delegate to target-specific implementations like `HTMLInputElement::ActivationBehavior()` (dom/html/HTMLInputElement.cpp) or `HTMLButtonElement::ActivationBehavior()` (dom/html/HTMLButtonElement.cpp).\\n\\n2. **In PostHandleEvent()** (dom/events/EventDispatcher.cpp:483-489): Called during the system event group dispatch. Element implementations like `Element::PostHandleEventForLinks()` (dom/base/Element.cpp:4318+) or `HTMLInputElement::PostHandleEvent()` (dom/html/HTMLInputElement.cpp:3896+) perform default actions such as navigating links or submitting forms.\\n\\n## System Event Group Dispatch\\nAfter the default event group completes, if the event is eligible, the dispatcher repeats the entire capture/target/bubble cycle for the system event group (lines 651-693). This is used for privileged, system-level event listeners that should not be affected by content listeners stopping propagation.\\n\\n## Key Files and Roles\\n\\n- **dom/events/EventDispatcher.cpp/h**: Main dispatcher orchestrating the entire flow\\n- **dom/events/EventListenerManager.cpp**: Manages registered listeners and invokes them\\n- **dom/events/Event.cpp**: DOM Event object (wraps WidgetEvent)\\n- **dom/events/EventStateManager.cpp**: Pre/post-event state management\\n- **dom/base/Element.cpp, Document.cpp, FragmentOrElement.cpp**: Event target implementations\\n- **dom/html/HTMLInputElement.cpp, HTMLButtonElement.cpp, etc.**: Element-specific event handling and default actions\\n- **layout/base/PresShell.cpp**: Integration point for layout-triggered events\\n- **widget/nsIWidget.cpp**: Platform widget event dispatch\\n\\nThe event dispatch chain ensures proper isolation of event phases, respects propagation stops, handles event retargeting for shadow DOM, and provides clear separation between listener invocation and default action execution.\"\n}\n",
